\tif obj == nil || obj.Value.IsNull() {\n334: \t\t// No need to encode anything: we'll just write it directly.\n335: \t\twrite(nil)\n336: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] %s: removing state object for %s\", logFuncName, absAddr)\n337: \t\treturn nil\n338: \t}\n339: \n340: \tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] %s: writing state object for %s\", logFuncName, absAddr)\n341: \n342: \tschema, currentVersion := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(absAddr.ContainingResource().Resource)\n343: \tif schema == nil {\n344: \t\t// It shouldn't be possible to get this far in any real scenario\n345: \t\t// without a schema, but we might end up here in contrived tests that\n346: \t\t// fail to set up their world properly.\n347: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to encode %s in state: no resource type schema available\", absAddr)\n348: \t}\n349: \n350: \tsrc, err := obj.Encode(schema.ImpliedType(), currentVersion)\n351: \tif err != nil {\n352: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to encode %s in state: %s\", absAddr, err)\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \twrite(src)\n356: \treturn nil\n357: }\n358: \n359: // planDestroy returns a plain destroy diff.\n360: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) planDestroy(ctx tfdiags.Diagnostics\n362: \tvar deferred *providers.Deferred\n363: \tvar plan *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n364: \n365: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n366: \tdeferralAllowed := is the\n463: \t\t// only valid value for a destroy plan.\n464: \t\tif !resp.PlannedState.IsNull() && deferred == nil {\n465: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n466: \t\t},\n487: \t\tPrivate:      resp.PlannedPrivate,\n488: \t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n489: \t}\n490: \n491: \treturn plan, deferred, diags\n492: }\n493: \n494: // planForget returns a planned change for an instance object into the set of\n542: // global planned changes.\n543: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) writeChange(ctx EvalContext, change *plans.ResourceInstanceChange, deposedKey states.DeposedKey) error {\n544: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n545: \n546: \tif change == nil {\n547: \t\t// Caller sets nil to indicate that we need to remove a change from\n548: \t\t// the set of changes.\n549: \t\tchanges.RemoveResourceInstanceChange(n.Addr, deposedKey)\n550: \t\treturn nil\n551: \t}\n552: \n553: \tif change.Addr.String() != n.Addr.String() || change.DeposedKey != deposedKey {\n554: \t\t// Should never happen, and indicates a bug in the caller.\n555: \t\tpanic(\"inconsistent address and/or deposed key in writeChange\")\n556: \t}\n557: \tif change.PrevRunAddr.Resource.Resource.Type == \"\" {\n558: \t\t// Should never happen, and indicates a bug in the caller.\n559: \t\t// (The change.Encode function actually has its own fixup to just\n560: \t\t// quietly make this match change.Addr in the incorrect case, but we\n561: \t\t// intentionally panic here in order to catch incorrect callers where\n562: \t\t// the stack trace will hopefully be actually useful. The tolerance\n563: \t\t// at the next layer down is mainly to accommodate sloppy input in\n564: \t\t// older tests.)\n565: \t\tpanic(\"unpopulated ResourceInstanceChange.PrevRunAddr in writeChange\")\n566: \t}\n567: \n568: \tchanges.AppendResourceInstanceChange(change)\n569: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n570: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] writeChange: recorded %s change for %s\", change.Action, n.Addr)\n571: \t} else {\n572: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] writeChange: recorded %s change for %s deposed object %s\", change.Action, n.Addr, deposedKey)\n573: \t}\n574: \n575: \treturn nil\n576: }\n577: \n578: // refresh does a refresh for a resource\n579: // if the second return value is non-nil, the refresh is deferred\n580: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) refresh(ctx EvalContext, deposedKey states.DeposedKey, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, deferralAllowed bool) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, *providers.Deferred, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n581: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n582: \tvar deferred *providers.Deferred\n583: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n584: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n585: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] NodeAbstractResourceInstance.refresh for %s\", absAddr)\n586: \t} else {\n587: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] NodeAbstractResourceInstance.refresh for %s (deposed object %s)\", absAddr, deposedKey)\n588: \t}\n589: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n590: \tif err != nil {\n591: \t\treturn state, deferred, diags.Append(err)\n592: \t}\n593: \t// If we have no state, we don't do any refreshing\n594: \tif state == nil {\n595: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] refresh: %s: no state, so not refreshing\", absAddr)\n596: \t\treturn state, deferred, diags\n597: \t}\n598: \n599: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(n.Addr.Resource.ContainingResource())\n600: \tif schema == nil {\n601: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n602: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type))\n603: \t\treturn state, deferred, diags\n604: \t}\n605: \n606: \tmetaConfigVal, metaDiags := n.providerMetas(ctx)\n607: \tdiags = diags.Append(metaDiags)\n608: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n609: \t\treturn state, deferred, diags\n610: \t}\n611: \n612: \t// Call pre-refresh hook\n613: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n614: \t\treturn h.PreRefresh(n.HookResourceIdentity(), deposedKey, state.Value)\n615: \t}))\n616: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n617: \t\treturn state, deferred, diags\n618: \t}\n619: \n620: \t// Refresh!\n621: \tpriorVal := state.Value\n622: \n623: \t// Unmarked before sending to provider\n624: \tvar priorMarks []cty.PathValueMarks\n625: \tpriorVal, priorMarks = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n626: \n627: \tvar resp providers.ReadResourceResponse\n628: \tif n.override != nil {\n629: \t\t// If we have an override set for this resource, we don't want to talk\n630: \t\t// to the provider so we'll just return whatever was in state.\n631: \t\tresp = providers.ReadResourceResponse{\n632: \t\t\tNewState: priorVal,\n633: \t\t}\n634: \t} else {\n635: \t\tresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n636: \t\t\tTypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n637: \t\t\tPriorState:   priorVal,\n638: \t\t\tPrivate:      state.Private,\n639: \t\t\tProviderMeta: metaConfigVal,\n640: \t\t\tClientCapabilities: providers.ClientCapabilities{\n641: \t\t\t\tDeferralAllowed: deferralAllowed,\n642: \t\t\t},\n643: \t\t})\n644: \n645: \t\t// If we don't support deferrals, but the provider reports a deferral and does not\n646: \t\t// emit any error level diagnostics, we should emit an error.\n647: \t\tif resp.Deferred != nil && !deferralAllowed && !resp.Diagnostics.HasErrors() {\n648: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(deferring.UnexpectedProviderDeferralDiagnostic(n.Addr))\n649: \t\t}\n650: \n651: \t\tif resp.Deferred != nil {\n652: \t\t\tdeferred = resp.Deferred\n653: \t\t}\n654: \t}\n655: \tif n.Config != nil {\n656: \t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(n.Config.Config, n.Addr.String())\n657: \t}\n658: \n659: \tdiags = diags.Append(resp.Diagnostics)\n660: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n661: \t\treturn state, deferred, diags\n662: \t}\n663: \n664: \tif resp.NewState == cty.NilVal {\n665: \t\t// This ought not to happen in real cases since it's not possible to\n666: \t\t// send NilVal over the plugin RPC channel, but it can come up in\n667: \t\t// tests due to sloppy mocking.\n668: \t\tpanic(\"new state is cty.NilVal\")\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \t// If we have deferred the refresh, we expect the new state not to be wholly known\n672: \t// and callers should be prepared to handle this.\n673: \tif !resp.NewState.IsWhollyKnown() && deferred == nil {\n674: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n675: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n676: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n677: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n678: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n679: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, \"The returned state contains unknown values\",\n680: \t\t\t),\n681: \t\t))\n682: \t}\n683: \n684: \tfor _, err := range resp.NewState.Type().TestConformance(schema.ImpliedType()) {\n685: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n686: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n687: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n688: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n689: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n690: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, tfdiags.FormatError(err),\n691: \t\t\t),\n692: \t\t))\n693: \t}\n694: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n695: \t\treturn state, deferred, diags\n696: \t}\n697: \n698: \tnewState := objchange.NormalizeObjectFromLegacySDK(resp.NewState, schema)\n699: \tif !newState.RawEquals(resp.NewState) {\n700: \t\t// We had to fix up this object in some way, and we still need to\n701: \t\t// accept any changes for compatibility, so all we can do is log a\n702: \t\t// warning about the change.\n703: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[WARN] Provider %q produced an invalid new value containing null blocks for %q during refresh\\n\", n.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr)\n704: \t}\n705: \n706: \tret := state.DeepCopy()\n707: \tret.Value = newState\n708: \tret.Private = resp.Private\n709: \n710: \t// We have no way to exempt provider using the legacy SDK from this check,\n711: \t// so we can only log inconsistencies with the updated state values.\n712: \t// In most cases these are not errors anyway, and represent \"drift\" from\n713: \t// external changes which will be handled by the subsequent plan.\n714: \tif errs := objchange.AssertObjectCompatible(schema, priorVal, ret.Value); len(errs) > 0 {\n715: \t\tvar buf strings.Builder\n716: \t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"[WARN] Provider %q produced an unexpected new value for %s during refresh.\", n.ResolvedProvider.Provider.String(), absAddr)\n717: \t\tfor _, err := range errs {\n718: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"\\n      - %s\", tfdiags.FormatError(err))\n719: \t\t}\n720: \t\tlog.Print(buf.String())\n721: \t}\n722: \n723: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n724: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n725: \t\treturn h.PostRefresh(n.HookResourceIdentity(), deposedKey, priorVal, ret.Value)\n726: \t}))\n727: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n728: \t\treturn ret, deferred, diags\n729: \t}\n730: \n731: \t// Mark the value with any prior marks from the state, and the marks from\n732: \t// the schema. This ensures we capture any marks from the last\n733: \t// configuration, as well as any marks from the schema which were not in\n734: \t// the prior state. New marks may appear when the prior state was from an\n735: \t// import operation, or if the provider added new marks to the schema.\n736: \tret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorMarks)\n737: \tif moreSensitivePaths := schema.SensitivePaths(ret.Value, nil); len(moreSensitivePaths) != 0 {\n738: \t\tret.Value = marks.MarkPaths(ret.Value, marks.Sensitive, moreSensitivePaths)\n739: \t}\n740: \n741: \treturn ret, deferred, diags\n742: }\n743: \n744: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n745: \tctx EvalContext,\n746: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n747: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n748: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n749: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n750: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, *providers.Deferred, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n751: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n752: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n753: \tvar deferred *providers.Deferred\n754: \n755: \tresource := n.Addr.Resource.Resource\n756: \tdeferralAllowed := ctx.Deferrals().DeferralAllowed()\n757: \n758: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n759: \tif err != nil {\n760: \t\treturn nil, nil, deferred, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n761: \t}\n762: \n763: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(resource)\n764: \tif schema == nil {\n765: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n766: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", resource.Type))\n767: \t\treturn nil, nil, deferred, keyData, diags\n768: \t}\n769: \n770: \t// If we're importing and generating config, generate it now.\n771: \tif n.Config == nil {\n772: \t\t// This shouldn't happen. A node that isn't generating config should\n773: \t\t// have embedded config, and the rest of Terraform should enforce this.\n774: \t\t// If, however, we didn't do things correctly the next line will panic,\n775: \t\t// so let's not do that and return an error message with more context.\n776: \n777: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n778: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n779: \t\t\t\"Resource has no configuration\",\n780: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Terraform attempted to process a resource at %s that has no configuration. Objects with this status\n1214: \t\t// cannot be used during expression evaluation, so the caller\n1215: \t\t// must _also_ record the returned change in the active plan,\n1216: \t\t// which the expression evaluator will use in preference to this\n1217: \t\t// incomplete value recorded in the state.\n1218: \t\tStatus:  states.ObjectPlanned,\n1219: \t\tValue:   plannedNewVal,\n1220: \t\tPrivate: plannedPrivate,\n1221: \t}\n1222: \n1223: \treturn plan, state, deferred, keyData, diags\n1224: }\n1225: \n1226: func (n *NodeAbstractResource) processIgnoreChanges(prior, config cty.Value, schema *configschema.Block) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1227: \t// ignore_changes only applies when an object already exists, since we\n1228: \t// can't ignore changes to a thing we've not created yet.\n1229: \tif prior.IsNull() {\n1230: \t\treturn config, nil\n1231: \t}\n1232: \n1233: \tignoreChanges := traversalsToPaths(n.Config.Managed.IgnoreChanges)\n1234: \tignoreAll := n.Config.Managed.IgnoreAllChanges\n1235: \n1236: \tif len(ignoreChanges) == 0 && !ignoreAll {\n1237: \t\treturn config, nil\n1238: \t}\n1239: \n1240: \tif ignoreAll {\n1241: \t\t// Legacy providers need up to clean up their invalid plans and ensure\n1242: \t\t// no changes are passed though, but that also means making an invalid\n1243: \t\t// config with computed values. In that case we just don't supply a\n1244: \t\t// schema and return the prior val directly.\n1245: \t\tif schema == nil {\n1246: \t\t\treturn prior, nil\n1247: \t\t}\n1248: \n1249: \t\t// If we are trying to ignore all attribute changes, we must filter\n1250: \t\t// computed attributes out from the prior state to avoid sending them\n1251: \t\t// to the provider as if they were included in the configuration.\n1252: \t\tret, _ := cty.Transform(prior, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1253: \t\t\tattr := schema.AttributeByPath(path)\n1254: \t\t\tif attr != nil && attr.Computed && !attr.Optional {\n1255: \t\t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n1256: \t\t\t}\n1257: \n1258: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1259: \t\t})\n1260: \n1261: \t\treturn ret, nil\n1262: \t}\n1263: \n1264: \tif prior.IsNull() || config.IsNull() {\n1265: \t\t// Ignore changes doesn't apply when we're creating for the first time.\n1266: \t\t// Proposed should never be null here, but if it is then we'll just let it be.\n1267: \t\treturn config, nil\n1268: \t}\n1269: \n1270: \tret, diags := processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config, ignoreChanges)\n1271: \n1272: \treturn ret, diags\n1273: }\n1274: \n1275: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1276: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1277: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1278: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1279: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1280: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1281: \t\tpaths[i] = path\n1282: \t}\n1283: \treturn paths\n1284: }\n1285: \n1286: func traversalToPath(traversal hcl.Traversal) cty.Path {\n1287: \tpath := make(cty.Path, len(traversal))\n1288: \tfor si, step := range traversal {\n1289: \t\tswitch ts := step.(type) {\n1290: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseRoot:\n1291: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1292: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1293: \t\t\t}\n1294: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseAttr:\n1295: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1296: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1297: \t\t\t}\n1298: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseIndex:\n1299: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.IndexStep{\n1300: \t\t\t\tKey: ts.Key,\n1301: \t\t\t}\n1302: \t\tdefault:\n1303: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unsupported traversal step %#v\", step))\n1304: \t\t}\n1305: \t}\n1306: \treturn path\n1307: }\n1308: \n1309: func processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1310: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1311: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1312: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1313: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1314: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1315: \t\t// key index.\n1316: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1317: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1318: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1319: \t}\n1320: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1321: \n1322: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1323: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1324: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1325: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1326: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1327: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1328: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1329: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1330: \t\tif ok {\n1331: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1332: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1333: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1334: \t\t\t}\n1335: \t\t}\n1336: \n1337: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1338: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. Any other intermediate index error\n1339: \t\t// means we wouldn't be able to apply the value below, so no need to\n1340: \t\t// record this.\n1341: \t\tp, err := icPath.Apply(prior)\n1342: \t\tif err != nil {\n1343: \t\t\tcontinue\n1344: \t\t}\n1345: \t\tc, err := icPath.Apply(config)\n1346: \t\tif err != nil {\n1347: \t\t\tcontinue\n1348: \t\t}\n1349: \n1350: \t\t// If this is a map, it is checking the entire map value for equality\n1351: \t\t// rather than the individual key. This means that the change is stored\n1352: \t\t// here even if our ignored key doesn't change. That is OK since it\n1353: \t\t// won't cause any changes in the transformation, but allows us to skip\n1354: \t\t// breaking up the maps and checking for key existence here too.\n1355: \t\tif !p.RawEquals(c) {\n1356: \t\t\t// there a change to ignore at this path, store the prior value\n1357: \t\t\tignoredValues = append(ignoredValues, ignoreChange{icPath, p, key})\n1358: \t\t}\n1359: \t}\n1360: \n1361: \tif len(ignoredValues) == 0 {\n1362: \t\treturn config, nil\n1363: \t}\n1364: \n1365: \tret, _ := cty.Transform(config, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1366: \t\t// Easy path for when we are only matching the entire value. The only\n1367: \t\t// values we break up for inspection are maps.\n1368: \t\tif !v.Type().IsMapType() {\n1369: \t\t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1370: \t\t\t\tif path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1371: \t\t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1372: \t\t\t\t}\n1373: \t\t\t}\n1374: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1375: \t\t}\n1376: \t\t// We now know this must be a map, so we need to accumulate the values\n1377: \t\t// key-by-key.\n1378: \n1379: \t\tif !v.IsNull() && !v.IsKnown() {\n1380: \t\t\t// since v is not known, we cannot ignore individual keys\n1381: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1382: \t\t}\n1383: \n1384: \t\t// The map values will remain as cty values, so we only need to store\n1385: \t\t// the marks from the outer map itself\n1386: \t\tv, vMarks := v.Unmark()\n1387: \n1388: \t\t// The configMap is the current configuration value, which we will\n1389: \t\t// mutate based on the ignored paths and the prior map value.\n1390: \t\tvar configMap map[string]cty.Value\n1391: \t\tswitch {\n1392: \t\tcase v.IsNull() || v.LengthInt() == 0:\n1393: \t\t\tconfigMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1394: \t\tdefault:\n1395: \t\t\tconfigMap = v.AsValueMap()\n1396: \t\t}\n1397: \n1398: \t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1399: \t\t\tif !path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1400: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1401: \t\t\t}\n1402: \n1403: \t\t\tif ignored.key.IsNull() {\n1404: \t\t\t\t// The map address is confirmed to match at this point,\n1405: \t\t\t\t// so if there is no key, we want the entire map and can\n1406: \t\t\t\t// stop accumulating values.\n1407: \t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1408: \t\t\t}\n1409: \t\t\t// Now we know we are ignoring a specific index of this map, so get\n1410: \t\t\t// the config map and modify, add, or remove the desired key.\n1411: \n1412: \t\t\t// We also need to create a prior map, so we can check for\n1413: \t\t\t// existence while getting the value, because Value.Index will\n1414: \t\t\t// return null for a key with a null value and for a non-existent\n1415: \t\t\t// key.\n1416: \t\t\tvar priorMap map[string]cty.Value\n1417: \n1418: \t\t\t// We need to drop the marks from the ignored map for handling. We\n1419: \t\t\t// don't need to store these, as we now know the ignored value is\n1420: \t\t\t// only within the map, not the map itself.\n1421: \t\t\tignoredVal, _ := ignored.value.Unmark()\n1422: \n1423: \t\t\tswitch {\n1424: \t\t\tcase ignored.value.IsNull() || ignoredVal.LengthInt() == 0:\n1425: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1426: \t\t\tdefault:\n1427: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = ignoredVal.AsValueMap()\n1428: \t\t\t}\n1429: \n1430: \t\t\tkey := ignored.key.AsString()\n1431: \t\t\tpriorElem, keep := priorMap[key]\n1432: \n1433: \t\t\tswitch {\n1434: \t\t\tcase !keep:\n1435: \t\t\t\t// this didn't exist in the old map value, so we're keeping the\n1436: \t\t\t\t// \"absence\" of the key by removing it from the config\n1437: \t\t\t\tdelete(configMap, key)\n1438: \t\t\tdefault:\n1439: \t\t\t\tconfigMap[key] = priorElem\n1440: \t\t\t}\n1441: \t\t}\n1442: \n1443: \t\tvar newVal cty.Value\n1444: \t\tswitch {\n1445: \t\tcase len(configMap) > 0:\n1446: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapVal(configMap)\n1447: \t\tcase v.IsNull():\n1448: \t\t\t// if the config value was null, and no values remain in the map,\n1449: \t\t\t// reset the value to null.\n1450: \t\t\tnewVal = v\n1451: \t\tdefault:\n1452: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapValEmpty(v.Type().ElementType())\n1453: \t\t}\n1454: \n1455: \t\tif len(vMarks) > 0 {\n1456: \t\t\tnewVal = newVal.WithMarks(vMarks)\n1457: \t\t}\n1458: \n1459: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1460: \t})\n1461: \treturn ret, nil\n1462: }\n1463: \n1464: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1465: // A previously evaluated configVal can be passed in, or a new one is generated\n1466: // from the resource configuration.\n1467: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) readDataSource(ctx EvalContext, *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) providerMetas(ctx EvalContext) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1620: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1621: \tmetaConfigVal := \t\t\t}\n1642: \t\t}\n1643: \t}\n1644: \treturn metaConfigVal, diags\n1645: }\n1646: \n1647: // planDataSource deals with the main part of the data resource lifecycle:\n1648: // either actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1649: //\n1650: // currentState is the current state for the data source, and the new state is\n1651: // returned. While data sources are read-only, we need to start with the prior\n1652: // state to determine if we have a change or not.  If we needed to read a new\n1653: // value, but it still matches the previous state, then we can record a NoNop\n1654: // change. If the states don't match then we record a Read change so that the\n1655: // new value is applied to the state.\n1656: //\n1657: // The cases where a data source will generate a planned change instead\n1658: // of finishing during the plan are:\n1659: //\n1660: //   - Its config has unknown values or it depends on a resource with pending changes.\n1661: //     (Note that every data source that is DeferredPrereq should also fit this description.)\n1662: //   - We attempted a read request, but the provider says we're deferred.\n1663: //   - It's nested in a check block, and should always read again during apply.\n1664: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) planDataSource(ctx EvalContext, checkRuleSeverity tfdiags.Severity, skipPlanChanges, dependencyDeferred bool) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, *providers.Deferred, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1665: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1666: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n1667: \tvar configVal cty.Value\n1668: \n1669: \tvar deferred *providers.Deferred\n1670: \tif dependencyDeferred {\n1671: \t\t// If a dependency of this data source was deferred, then we're going\n1672: \t\t// to end up deferring this whatever happens. So, our default status\n1673: \t\t// is deferred. \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n1703: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n1704: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n1705: \t)\n1706: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n1707: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1708: \t\treturn nil, schema).InConfigBody(n.Config.Config, n.Addr.String()),\n1716: \t)\n1717: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1718: \t\treturn nil, nil, deferred, keyData, diags\n1719: \t}\n1720: \tunmarkedConfigVal, is\n1725: \t\t// that the data source fails to load its data. Normally, this would\n1726: \t\t// cancel the entire plan and this error message would bubble its way\n1727: \t\t// back up to the user.\n1728: \t\t//\n1729: \t\t// But, if we are in a check block then we don't want this data block to\n1730: \t\t// cause the plan to fail. We also need to report a status on the data\n1731: \t\t// block so the check processing later on knows whether to attempt to\n1732: \t\t// process the checks. Either we'll report the data block as failed\n1733: \t\t// if/when we load the data block later, or we want to report it as a\n1734: \t\t// success overall.\n1735: \t\t//\n1736: \t\t// Therefore, we create a deferred function here that will check if the\n1737: \t\t// status for the check has been updated yet, and if not we will set it\n1738: \t\t// to be StatusPass. if so\n2103: // executes the provisioners for a resource and returns an updated error if\n2104: // provisioning fails.\n2105: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) evalApplyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, createNew bool, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2106: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2107: \n2108: \tif state == nil {\n2109: \n2160: // filterProvisioners filters the provisioners on the resource to only\n2161: // the provisioners specified by the \"when\" option.\n2162: func filterProvisioners(configured []*configs.Provisioner, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) []*configs.Provisioner {\n2163: \tif len(configured) == 0 {\n2164: \t\treturn nil\n2165: \t}\n2166: \n2167: \tresult := make([]*configs.Provisioner, 0, len(configured))\n2168: \tfor _, p := range configured {\n2169: \t\tif p.When == when {\n2170: \t\t\tresult = append(result, p)\n2171: \t\t}\n2172: \t}\n2173: \n2174: \treturn result\n2175: }\n2176: \n2177: // applyProvisioners executes the provisioners for a resource.\n2178: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state
